## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves determining the rate law for a chemical reaction where dA/dt depends on concentration A and possibly time t. The rate of change of concentration typically follows power-law dependence on concentration (nth-order kinetics), but may involve more complex mechanisms like autocatalysis, reversible reactions, or time-dependent external influences.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to concentration squared)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reactions with equilibrium)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product catalyzes its own formation)
- Second-order with equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (quadratic rate expression)
- Time-dependent forcing with decay: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (reaction with time-dependent source/sink)
- Mixed time-concentration dependence: dA_dt = c0 * A * t**c1 (time-dependent rate coefficient)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order kinetics with baseline)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (substrate inhibition or saturation)
- Damped oscillatory rate: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A * sin(c2 * t) (periodic modulation of rate)
- Competitive pathway: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A**c2 (multiple reaction pathways)
- Square-root kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5 (half-order reaction, surface-mediated)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope Ôćĺ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects Ôćĺ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay Ôćĺ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior Ôćĺ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects Ôćĺ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence (no explicit time) Ôćĺ classical rate law dA/dt = k*A^n, look for power-law in A
- Linear dependence on A with nonzero intercept Ôćĺ reversible reaction or constant source/sink term
- Quadratic in A (A*(c-A) form) Ôćĺ autocatalytic or second-order opposing reactions
- Explicit time dependence in rate Ôćĺ time-varying external conditions (temperature ramp, photochemistry, catalyst deactivation)
- Rate proportional to A*t or A*f(t) Ôćĺ time-dependent rate constant, possibly Arrhenius with programmed temperature
- Fractional power of A Ôćĺ surface-catalyzed reactions or complex mechanisms with quasi-steady-state intermediates
- Rate expression with A in denominator Ôćĺ inhibition or saturation effects from Langmuir-Hinshelwood mechanism
- Sign of dA/dt uniformly negative Ôćĺ consumption/decay reaction; sign change Ôćĺ reversible or oscillatory system
